| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox Content Security Policy Enforcement Audit

## Your Task

Audit the Content Security Policy (CSP) enforcement infrastructure in Firefox. Find all C++ source files in `mozilla-firefox/firefox` under `dom/security/` that implement CSP parsing, evaluation, and violation reporting. Specifically: 1. The file that defines `nsCSPParser` — the CSP directive parser. 2. The file that implements `nsCSPContext` — the main CSP context that holds policies. 3. The file that implements CSP violation reporting (`nsCSPUtils` or similar). 4. The header file that declares the `nsIContentSecurityPolicy` XPCOM interface. 5. The file under `dom/security/` that performs script-src evaluation for inline scripts. Report each file path and its primary class or function.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've completed the CSP enforcement infrastructure audit for Firefox. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I've identified all five major components of Firefox's CSP enforcement system in the `dom/security/` directory:

### 1. **nsCSPParser** (`dom/security/nsCSPParser.h/cpp`)
- The CSP directive parser class that tokenizes and parses CSP policy strings
- Main entry point: `parseContentSecurityPolicy()` static method

### 2. **nsCSPContext** (`dom/security/nsCSPContext.h/cpp`)  
- The main CSP context class implementing the `nsIContentSecurityPolicy` XPCOM interface
- Holds and enforces parsed policies at runtime
- Key method `ShouldLoad()` at line 144 evaluates content load requests
- `ReportInlineViolation()` at line 563 handles violation reporting

### 3. **nsCSPUtils** (`dom/security/nsCSPUtils.h/cpp`)
- Implements CSP violation reporting and utility functions
- Defines directive classes including `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective` which evaluates script-src for inline scripts
- Contains source matching logic and violation event data structures

### 4. **nsIContentSecurityPolicy** (`dom/interfaces/security/nsIContentSecurityPolicy.idl`)
- XPCOM interface declaration for CSP components
- Defines CSP directive enums and the ShouldLoad method interface

### 5. **Script-src Inline Evaluation**
- Occurs in `nsCSPContext.cpp` through the `ShouldLoad()` → `permitsInternal()` → directive evaluation flow
- `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective` class checks for 'unsafe-inline', nonces, hashes, and 'strict-dynamic'
- Violations are reported through `ReportInlineViolation()` which fires SecurityPolicyViolationEvent and sends HTTP reports

Whether 'unsafe-inline' keyword is present\\n   - Whether the script has a valid nonce matching the policy\\n   - Whether the script hash matches a policy-allowed hash\\n   - Whether 'strict-dynamic' is present (affecting external vs inline)\\n4. **Violation Reporting:** If blocked, `ReportInlineViolation()` is called to:\\n   - CSP Context/Policy Enforcer - `dom/security/nsCSPContext.h` and `dom/security/nsCSPContext.cpp`\\n**Primary Class:** `nsCSPContext` (implements `nsIContentSecurityPolicy` interface)\\n**Responsibility:** Main CSP context that holds parsed policies and enforces them at runtime\\n**Key Methods:**\\n- `ShouldLoad()` (line 144 in .cpp): XPCOM interface method that evaluates whether a load is permitted by CSP\\n- `permitsInternal()`: Core evaluation logic for checking if a resource load violates CSP\\n- `ReportInlineViolation()` (line 563 in .cpp): Helper method to report inline script/style violations\\n- `GatherSecurityPolicyViolationEventData()`: Constructs violation event data\\n- `SendReports()`: Dispatches CSP violation reports\\n- `allowsAllInlineBehavior()`: Checks if a directive allows all inline behavior (e.g., 'unsafe-inline')\\n\\nThe context manages multiple CSP policies, handles violation reporting to report-uri endpoints, fires SecurityPolicyViolationEvent events, and provides console logging for violations.\\n\\n### 3. CSP Utilities & Directives - `dom/security/nsCSPUtils.h` and `dom/security/nsCSPUtils.cpp`\\n**Primary Classes:**\\n- `nsCSPDirective`: Base class for all CSP directives\\n- `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective`: Specialized class for script-src directive that can restrict script elements, event handlers, and workers\\n- `nsCSPStyleSrcDirective`: For style-src directives\\n- `nsCSPChildSrcDirective`: For child-src directive (backwards compatibility)\\n- Source classes: `nsCSPHostSrc`, `nsCSPSchemeSrc`, `nsCSPKeywordSrc`, `nsCSPNonceSrc`, `nsCSPHashSrc`\\n\\n**Responsibilities:**\\n- Define CSP source matching logic (permits(), allows() methods)\\n- Implement directive-specific behavior (e.g., script-src handling multiple fallback rules)\\n- Handle CSP-related logging and localized error messages\\n- Provide violation data structures\\n\\n**Script-src Evaluation Functions:**\\n- `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective::permits()`: Evaluates if a script source is allowed\\n- `nsCSPDirective::allows()`: Checks if a directive allows specific keywords, nonces, or hashes\\n- `allowsAllInlineBehavior()`: Determines if inline scripts are permitted (checks for 'unsafe-inline', nonces, hashes, or strict-dynamic)\\n\\n### 4. XPCOM Interface Declaration - `dom/interfaces/security/nsIContentSecurityPolicy.idl`\\n**Primary Interface:** `nsIContentSecurityPolicy`\\n**Responsibility:** Defines the XPCOM interface for CSP components\\n**Key Methods:**\\n- `ShouldLoad()`: Policy check method called at content load time\\n- Multiple directive enums (CSPDirective): SCRIPT_SRC_DIRECTIVE, SCRIPT_SRC_ELEM_DIRECTIVE, SCRIPT_SRC_ATTR_DIRECTIVE, etc.\\n\\n## Script-src Evaluation for Inline Scripts\\n\\nInline script evaluation occurs primarily in `dom/security/nsCSPContext.cpp` through the following flow:\\n\\n1. **Entry Point:** `ShouldLoad()` method (line 144) receives load requests\\n2. **Policy Matching:** `permitsInternal()` matches the content type to appropriate CSP directives (script-src, script-src-elem, etc.)\\n3. **Inline Script Check:** For inline scripts, the evaluation checks:\\n   - Whether 'unsafe-inline' keyword is present\\n   - Whether the script has a valid nonce matching the policy\\n   - Whether the script hash matches a policy-allowed hash\\n   - Whether 'strict-dynamic' is present (affecting external vs inline)\\n4. **Violation Reporting:** If blocked, `ReportInlineViolation()` is called to:\\n   - Create violation event data via `GatherSecurityPolicyViolationEventData()`\\n   - Fire SecurityPolicyViolationEvent to the page\\n   - Send reports to configured report-uri/report-to endpoints\\n\\nThe `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective` class (in nsCSPUtils.h/cpp) holds the actual script-src policy sources and implements the evaluation logic for determining whether inline scripts are allowed based on keywords, nonces, and hashes.\\n\\n## Integration Architecture\\n\\nThe CSP enforcement pipeline:\\n1. **Parsing Stage:** CSP header/meta tags \u2192 `nsCSPParser::parseContentSecurityPolicy()` \u2192 `nsCSPPolicy` object\\n2. **Storage Stage:** Policy stored in `nsCSPContext` instance associated with Document\\n3. **Enforcement Stage:** When content loads, `nsCSPService` calls `nsCSPContext::ShouldLoad()`\\n4. **Evaluation Stage:** `nsCSPContext` queries appropriate directive (e.g., `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective`) to determine permissibility\\n5. **Reporting Stage:** If violation, `ReportInlineViolation()` dispatches events and HTTP reports\\n\\n## File Relationships\\n\\n- `nsCSPParser` is instantiated by and calls back to `nsCSPContext` during parsing\\n- `nsCSPContext` holds instances of `nsCSPPolicy` which contain `nsCSPDirective` objects\\n- `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective` and other directive classes inherit from `nsCSPDirective` and hold `nsCSPBaseSrc` objects representing individual sources\\n- All three main implementation files (`nsCSPParser.cpp`, `nsCSPContext.cpp`, `nsCSPUtils.cpp`) are compiled together as part of the dom/security module\\n- The XPCOM interface in `.idl` file is the C++ definition language used to generate bindings\"\n}\n",
